< Rating>

< text>
Hands down the BEST food and best restauraunt I've eaten in a while!!

My girlfriend and I found this place on a whim. We were going to go to another restauraunt in the shopping center, but last second changed our minds and decided to give Asaka a try.

Immediately we were greeted by the SWEETEST server ever, Nana. She was beyond friendly, professional, and had an amazing attitude. I am vegetarian so she helped me out with plenty of options and substitutions.

We sat outside on the patio. Covid measures were practiced appropriately. The food was colorful, gorgeous and down right delicious.

We had miso soup and fried tofu for appetizers, the sushi burritothe hungry tiger roll and also the bento box lunch which the bento lunch special was only 12 dollars and filled me up.

Pair a couple of sapporos and a green tea I've cream, we left happy as heck (and a little fatter, but hey, ya gotta spoil yourself every now and then)

Anyone who is looking for a safe place to go to with a pretty view and good food now that outdoor dining is back, go here!!</text>

<Date>1573155926265<//Date><Review>I am a huge fan of this place. Full disclosure I have been coming to the PV location with my family for years. The staff is amazing, friendly, helpful, and attentive plus the prices are reasonable, and the view is pretty stellar.

Located in Golden Cove on PV Dr West there is plenty of parking but it can get congested due to the Trader Joes and other restaurants and businesses in the center.

There is indoor and outdoor seating with a great view of the ocean. When the weather gets cooler there is a large fire pit that keeps things toasty.

The lunch specials are great and are served every day until 4:30 pm. You can get a Bento box with soup and white or brown rice or a Sushi combo with soup - all options under $16.

On this trip, we ordered a bunch of specials: the Chefs sashimi combo, spicy tuna jalapenos, scallop roll, a rice-less designer roll, beer, and sake. The grand total was under $70. Not bad for 2 people.<//Review>< user_name>

<userid>114350511464802415942</userid><user_name>Clarice O Hanmal< /user_name><time>1517465915397<//time>< rating>
4<//rating>
<review>I have been here last month for lunch during Restaurant Week, and I really enjoyed this place. It is located in a very beautiful small castle built in 1930, that works also as a hotel today. Food is very tasteful, service is impeccable and the price is pretty much fair. The restaurant is very small, you should reserve a table by the window and prove their delicious creme brulee. The only reason that I do not give five stars is that I think they need a revitalization, a kind of update without losing the historic style.<//review>< pics>

<Rate>3</Rate><Review>Food was good and afternoon tea was nice.  The plan was to check out Julia's for the Restaurant Week menu, but they do not serve the lunch menu on weekends. This was very disappointing because this was not stated on the posted lunch menu or Julia's Restaurant Week page.

As typical for restaurants that do not specialize in steaks, ordering medium-rare gets you a solid medium. (This is a trick we learned long ago after getting tired of eating almost well-done steaks when ordering medium and not wanting to contribute to food waste.)

The black tea was subpar and slightly bitter.  On the bright side, the African root tea was a great discovery. Scones and Devonshire cream we're delightful- it's half of the reason I love afternoon tea.

Pros: solid spot for afternoon tea, although pricy (~$50/person after tax and tip)

<pictures>None</pictures><time>1548906671663< /time><UserId.>111793850915333684321<//UserId.><user_name>Mary O'sullivan< /user_name>< text>
Historic building enhances the entire experience. Restaurant Week $20 lunch was enjoyed by all and even our group's grump had to admit it was good value. Definitely worth a visit especially with out_of-town guests and architecture fans. Wheelchair accessible via street-level door leading into a basement tunnel to a smallish elevator. Cool!  Super-convenient venue for romantic dinner or any type of larger event requiring a stage and/or dance floor. Lovely courtyard garden too. Parking for non-members is $10 and we were glad we paid up and were able to relax and enjoy our visit unpressured by need to feed the meter. Great place. No, I am not a member or even a regular, but I would if my budget permitted and if I didn't live only a few blocks away.

< Review>
We were staying at the Berkeley City Club hotel, and it was pouring rain, so we decided to have a fancy dinner at Julia's. It definitely fits the bill for a couple or a small group looking to have a nice evening. Nothing about this restaurant stands out other than the neat historic building it's in, but nothing about Julia's will offend anyone, either, unless you're turned off by a menu that has only one vegetarian entree and no vegan entree options. The service was stellar. Attentive, friendly, and thoughtful, without being obtrusive - the staff are all definitely pros. The food was prepared well, and met our expectations based on the menu. There's nothing exciting or amazing on the menu, but it's nice. We ended up spending $125 for two entrees, one appetizer, one soup, a bottle of wine, and one dessert to split. If you enjoy spending time with the person or people you're having dinner with, and you don't need vegan meal options, then I'm willing to bet you would have a lovely time at Julia's. However, I wouldn't recommend that anyone should go out of their way to dine at Julia's. There are so many other options in Berkeley. And, if you're a foodie specifically looking to experience amazing food, you would probably be disappointed.</Review>

< Review>
It's busy at lunch. Food is not exactly Vietnamese Authentic. They serve egg rolls that are huge, but no lettuce wraps or Vietnamese sauce to go with them. Instead packets of sweet and sour sauce. The Pho is okay but wow - huge portion. The bowl is massive. Soup tastes fine but I guess I'm a bit spoiled being from Southern California where we have  large population of Vietnamese people, meaning a lot of restaurants to choose from. The owners are really nice here, treating customers well. Lots of smiles. I reccomend this restaurant.<//Review>

Alex Camacho<//name>
< review>
Great location, I often go during the week for lunch. Fairly quick service and reasonable prices for downtown. I almost always get a pork banh mi - it's simple, tasty, and only about $7. Colleagues often get the pho and are always complimenting the broth.

Restaurant keeps lunch hours and is popular - very common for a line of 8 or so to form in the middle of the small shop. While there are a few hidden tables in the back, you might want to consider going in early or holding off for a bit to avoid the noon crowd. You can also order food to-go and call in your order ahead.<//review>

< review>
Decent enough pho, but I went there today for the banh mi. Most places charge $2 or so for theirs; Kim's is $3.50, but the size of the sandwich is pretty darn big - definitely bigger than a $2 sandwich. Only quibble is that the bread needs to be crustier - the rolls were a little soft. And more pickled veggies would be great. But the bbq chicken was excellent and the sandwich was packed with it. Quick service, too.

Definitely the best banh mi near the Capitol, and a great place for lunch.< /review>
